[S─Бvitr─л S┼лry─Б.тАФ─Бtmad─Бivatam (10. yakс╣гman─Б┼Ыan─л; 11. dampatyoс╕е paripanthin─Б┼Ыan─л; 36 тМК?тМЛ dev─Бn ast─Бut). тМКAs to the foregoing statements, see above, page 739, ┬╢’s 8, 4, 5.тМЛ ─Бnuс╣гс╣нubham: 5, 6, 12, 31, 37, 39, 40. jagat─л (37, 39 bhurik triс╣гс╣нubh); 9. 3-av. 6-p. vir─Бс╕Н atyaс╣гс╣нi; 13, 14, 17-19, [34, 36, 38] 41, 42, 49, 61, 70, 74, 75. triс╣гс╣нubh; 15, 51. bhurij; 20. purast─Бdbс╣Ыhat─л; 13 тМК!тМЛ, 24, 25, 32, 33 тМК!тМЛ purobс╣Ыhat─л; [26. 3-p. vir─Бс╣З n─Бma g─Бyatr─л;] 33. vir─Бс╕Н ─Бst─Бrapan╠Дkti; 35. purobс╣Ыhat─л triс╣гс╣нubh; 43. triс╣гс╣нubgarbh─Б pan╠Дkti; 44. prast─Бrapan╠Дkti; [47. pathy─Бbс╣Ыhat─л; ] 48. sataс╕еpan╠Дkti тМКsee under the verseтМЛ; тМК50. upariс╣гс╣н─Бdbс╣Ыtat─л nicс╣Ыt;] 52. vir─Бс╣н paroс╣гс╣Зih; 59, 60, 62. pathy─Бpan╠Дkti; [68. pura-uс╣гс╣Зih;] 69. 3-av. 6-p. ati┼Ыakvar─л; 71. bс╣Ыhat─л.]

Comment

The Anukramaс╣З─л, as we have it, omits the description of several of the verses (26, 34, 36, 38, 47, 50, 68); тМКand, on the other hand, it defines verses 13 and 33 each twice, each once right and once wrong;тМЛ and it mixes the order of others тМКcompare Whitney’s remarks, above, page 739, If ┬╢3, and mine, page 740, topтМЛ.

The verses (except 50, 58) of this anuv─Бka or hymn are found also in P─Бipp. xviii. (for slight differences of order, see under the verses). тМКAbout a dozen verses of this anuv─Бka or hymn also occur in the RV. wedding-hymn, x. 85.тМЛ Only one verse (47) is used by V─Бit., but nearly all by K─Бu┼Ы.

Translations

Translated: parts, of course, by the RV. translators; and the parts peculiar to our text by Ludwig, p. 472; and, as AV. hymn, by Weber (as above), Ind. Stud. v. 204-217. For vss. 59-62, see Bloomfield, AJP. xi. 336-341, or JAOS. xv., p. xliv, = PAOS. for Oct. 1890.

Translation
  1. For thee in the beginning they carried about S┼лry─Б, together with the
    bridal-car; mayest thou, O Agni, give to us husbands the wife, together
    with progeny.
Notes

The verse is RV. x. 85. 38, RV. reading p├║naс╕е for s├б naс╕е in c.
All our mss. accent in d ├бgne, but it has been emended to agne
in our edition. Ppp. agrees with RV. in having in c punaс╣г pat-.
тМКCf. PGS. i. 7. 3; MP. i. 5. 3; MGS. i. 11. 12 b, and p. 150.тМЛ K─Бu┼Ы.
78. 10 quotes this verse with 45 below, both preceded by vi. 78. 1, and
followed by a long prose-passage, when the pair approach the priest to
receive a sort of baptism.

Griffith

For thee with bridal train they first escorted Surya to her home, Give to the husband in return, Agni, the wife with future sons.

Translation
  1. Agni hath given back the spouse, together with life-time, with
    splendor; of long life-time, may he who is the husband of her live a
    hundred autumns.
Notes

and p. 152.тМЛ The combination y├бс╕е p├бtiс╕е in c is assured by Pr─Бt.
ii. 70.

Griffith

Agni hath given the bride again with splendour and a lengthened. life. Long-lived be he who is her lord: a hundred autumns let him live.

Translation
  1. Soma gave to the Gandharva; the Gandharva gave to Agni; both wealth
    and sons hath Agni given to me, likewise this woman.
Notes

Is RV. x. 85. 41, without variant. Found also in MB. (i. 1. 7) and HGS.
(i. 20. 2): in the latter, with very different readings: soma тАШdad─Бd
gajidharv─Бya gandharva тАШgnaye тАШdad─Бt: pa┼Ы┼лс╣Е┼Ы ca mahyam putr─Бс╣Е┼Ы ca тАЩgnir
dad─Бty atho tv─Бm. тМКCf. MP. i. 3. 2; MGS. i. 10. 10 a, and p. 157; also
Wint., p. 48.тМЛ

Griffith

Soma to the Gandharva, and to Agni the Gandharva gave. Now, Agni hath bestowed on me riches and sons and this my bride.

  1. Your favor hath come, O ye (two) of abundant good things (?
    v─Бj├нn─лvasu); [our] desires have rested in [your] hearts, O A┼Ыvins;
    ye have been twin keepers, O lords of beauty; may we, being dear, attain
    favorers (aryam├бn) of our homes (? d├║rya).
Notes

The verse is RV. x. 40. 12, RV., however, reading ayaс╣Еsata at end of
b. тМКMP. i. 7. 11 follows the RV. text, but with k─Бm─Бс╣Е for k─Бm─Бs:
cf. Wint., p. 70.тМЛ More points than one in the translation are doubtful.

Griffith

Your favouring grace hath come, ye who are rich in spoil! Asvins, your longings are stored up within your hearts. Ye, Lords of Splendour have become our twofold guard: may we as dear friends reach the dwelling of the friend.

режрем рд╕рд╛ рдордиреНрджрд╕рд╛рдирд╛рдордирд╕рд╛ ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. Do thou (f.), rejoicing with propitious mind, assign wealth having
    all heroes, to be extolled; an easy crossing (t─лrth├б), well provided
    with drink, O lords (du.) of beauty; do ye smite away the pillar
    standing in the road, [namely] disfavor.
Notes

This verse is altered from RV. x. 40. 13 in a strange and senseless
manner. RV. reads for a, b t─Б╠Б mandas─Бn─Б╠Б m├бnuс╣гo duroс╣З├б ─Б╠Б dhatt├бс╣Б
ray├нс╣Б sah├бv─лraс╣Б vacasy├бve, thus making the verse concern the A┼Ыvins
throughout; who is our ’thou’ (s─Б╠Б) does not appear. In c the sense
is destroyed by altering the RV. verb kс╣Ыt├бm (as if it were
misunderstood for a participle) to sug├бm; and in d patheс╣гс╣нh─Б╠Бm
(p. patheре░sth─Б╠Бm) is turned to p├бthiс╣гс╣нh─Бm (p. p├бthiре░sth─Бm) and
accented as if it were a superlative; тМКcf. the confusion at vi. 28. 1тМЛ.
The verse is used also in the ─Аpast. s┼лtra (Wint., p. 68 тМКMP. i. 6.
12тМЛ), with da┼Ыav─лram in b as its only variant from RV. Ppp.
appears to read with our text. The verse lacks two syllables of being a
real jagat─л. In K─Бu┼Ы. 77. 8 the verse is directed to be used on
arriving at a ford or river-crossing on the bridal journey.

Griffith

Thou, Dame, rejoicing, take with kindly spirit wealth worthy to be famed, with all thy heroes. Give, Lords of Light a fair ford, good to drink at: remove the spiteful stump that blocks the pathway.

Translation
  1. What herbs [there are], what streams, what fields, what forestsтАФlet
    these, O bride, defend from the demon thee, possessing progeny, for thy
    husband.

Griffith

May all the Rivers, all the Plants, may all the Forests, all the Fields, O Bride, protect thee from the fiend, guard his sons’ mother for her lord.

    takes no harm, [but] finds others’ goods.

Our feet are on this pleasant path, easy to travel, bringing bliss, Whereon no hero suffers harm, which wins the wealth of other men.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Pray hear ye now of me, O men, by what blessing (─Б┼Ы├нs) the two
    spouses attain what is agreeable (v─Бm├б): what Gandharvas [there are]
    and heavenly Apsarases, who stand upon these forest trees
    (v─Бnaspaty├б), let them be pleasant unto this bride; let them not
    injure the bridal-car as it is driven.
Notes

The last four padas form a verse also in the ─Аpast. text (Wint., p. 70
тМКMP. i. 7. 8тМЛ), where for our d is read eс╣г├║ vс╣Ыkс╣г├йс╣гu v─Бnaspaty├йс╣гv
─Б╠Бsate, further ┼Ыiv─Б╠Бs (for syon─Б╠Бs) and vadhv─Б├м in e, and
┼лhy├бm─Бn─Бm in f. In TS. iii. 2. 8тБ┤ is found the phrase y├бm ─Б┼Ы├нr─Б
d├бmpat─л v─Бm├бm a┼Ыnut├бс╕е, and ─Б┼Ы─лrd─Бy─Б╠Б d├бmpat─л v─Бm├бm a┼Ыnut─Бm. The verse
is to be used, according to K─Бu┼Ы. 77. 9, when the bridal train passes
great trees. The Anukr. тМКappears to scan as 9 + 12: 11 + 12: 11 + 11 =
66; but p─Бda a is essentially defectiveтМЛ. All our mss. тМКand SPP’s
authoritiesтМЛ read in e te, which our edition emends to t├й; тМКbut
SPP. reads te, construing a-d together, and e-f separately:
‘unto thee, the bride here’; which seems hardтМЛ. Ppp. combines in c
gandharv─Б тАЩps-.

Griffith

Here these my words, ye men, the benediction through which the wedded pair have found high fortune. May the divine Apsarases, Gandharvas, all they who are these fruitful trees’ protectors, Regard this bride with their auspicious, favour, nor harm the nuptial pomp as it advances.

Translation
  1. What y├бkс╣гmas go to the bride’s brilliant (candr├б) car among the
    people, let the worshipful gods conduct those back whence they came.

Griffith

Consumptions, which, through various folk, attack the bride’s resplendent train, These let the holy Gods again bear to the place from which they sprang.

  1. Propitious hath this woman come to the home; Dh─Бtar appointed this
    world (sphere) to her; her let Aryaman, Bhaga, both A┼Ыvins, Praj─Бpati,
    increase with progeny.

Griffith

She hath come home this dame come home to bless us: this her appointed world hath Dhatar shown her. So may Prajapati, and both the Asvins, Aryaman, Bhaga gladden her with offspring.

Translation
  1. [As] a soulful cultivated field hath this woman come; in her
    here, O men, scatter ye seed; she shall give birth to progeny for you
    from her belly (vakс╣г├бс╣З─Бs), bearing the exuded (dugdh├б) sperm of the
    male (с╣Ыс╣гabh├б).
Notes

A couple of our mss. (тМКE.тМЛD.) read asy─Б╠Бm in c. The first p─Бda is
capable of being compressed into 11 syllables, but with violence. Ppp.
has for b yasy─Бn naro vapanta b─лjam asy─Бс╕е, and in c janay─Бt.

тМКThe likening of the woman to the field is very familiar later: cf. Manu
ix. 33 f. Cf. also the

╬╝╬▒╧Д╧Бс╜╕╧В с╝Д╧Б╬┐╧Е╧Б╬▒╬╜ Aeschylus (Septem, 753); Sophocles’ с╝А╧Б╧О╧Г╬╣╬╝╬┐╬╣ ╬│с╜░╧Б ╧Зс╝Б╧Д╬н╧Б╧Й╬╜
╬╡с╝░╧Гс╜╢╬╜ ╬│╧Н╬▒╬╣ (Ant., 569); Eurip. Phoen. 18; etc. My colleague, Professor
George F. Moore, calls my attention to Koran ii. 22, “Your women are
your plow-land,” in Arabic, с╕еarth.тАФGriffith’s (not very close) version
suggests a different interpretation: he takes dugdh├бm as ‘milk’ of the
maternal breast. Perhaps after all we should (with W.) join it with
r├йtas, and in the sense of ‘milked’; but with this difference, that it
refers to the r├йtas which is “milked” as a result of the action
implied in p├бso n├н galgal─лti dh─Б╠Бrak─Б at VS. xxiii. 22. Mah─лdhara says
v─лryaс╣Б kс╣гarati (cf. kс╣г─лram).тАФThis interpretation is fortified by the
use of dhayati at RV. i. 179. 4, L├│p─Бmudr─Б vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гaс╣Зaс╣Б (nad├бс╣Б) dhayati
┼Ыvas├бntam.тМЛ

Griffith

This dame hath come, an animated corn-field: there sow, thou man, the seed of future harvest. She from her teeming side shall bear thee children, and feed them from the fountain of her bosom.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Let your wave smite up the pegs; O waters, release the yoke-ropes
    (y├│ktra); let not the two inviolable [kine], not evil-doing, free
    from guilt, come upon what is unpropitious (? ├б┼Ыuna).
Notes

The verse is RV. iii. 33. 13, which, however, reads ┼Ы┼л╠Бnam for ├б┼Ыunam
in d, and vy├иnas─Б for -s─Бu in d; and Ppp. agrees with RV.
тМКW’s “[kine]” seems to overlook the gender of aghny─Б├║: see
Griffith’s note, p. 174.тМЛ K─Бu┼Ы. 77. 15 makes the verse accompany the
sprinkling of the car and unyoking of the oxen at the end of the bridal
journey.

Griffith

So let your wave bear up the pins, and ye, O Waters, spare the thongs; And never may the holy pair, sinless and innocent, suffer harm.

Whitney
Translation
  1. With an eye not terrible, not husband-slaying, pleasant, helpful
    (┼Ыagm├б), very propitious, of easy control (suy├бma) for the houses,
    hero-bearing, loving brothers-in-law (?), with favoring mindтАФmay we
    thrive together with thee.
Notes

The concluding word is here rendered as the text gives it, but there is
little question that it ought to be emended (with Ppp.) to -m─Бn─Бс╕е, as
qualifying ‘we.’ This verse and the next are a sort of duplication and
variation of RV. x. 85. 44; our a here is nearly the same with the
first p─Бda of that verse, which, however, reads edhi for our syon─Б.
Ppp. makes our 17 c, d and 18 c, d change places, reading for
the former v─лras┼лr devak─Бm─Б syon─Бс╣Б tvedhiс╣г─лmahi sumanasyam─Бn─Бс╕е. Our
mss. are divided in c between devс╣Ы╠Бk─Бm─Б and dev├бk-, the majority
(not Bp.Bs.p.m.E.O.D.) having, with RV. and Ppp., the latter, which is
therefore more probably the true reading. Ppp. has in a (like RV.)
edhi but with syon─Б after it тМКa “blend-reading” such as the Vulgate
shows at vs. 18?тМЛ; and, in b, s┼лyam─Б gс╣Ыheс╣гu. тМКCf. MP. i. 1. 4;
MGS. i. 10. 6, and p. 146.тМЛ The verse accompanies in K─Бu┼Ы. 77. 22 the
leading of the bride thrice about the fire. PCS. i. 4. 16 and HGS. i.
20.2 have it in its RV. form, with slight variants in HGS. Our verse (11

  • 11: 7 + 13 = 42) is metrically much too irregular to be set down as
    simply a triс╣гс╣нubh.
Griffith

Not evil-eyed no slayer of thy husband, be strong, mild, kind, and gentle to thy household. Mother of heroes, love thy husband’s father: be happy, and through thee may we too prosper.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Not brother-in-law-slaying, not husband-slaying be thou here,
    propitious to the cattle, of easy control, very splendid, having
    progeny, hero-bearing, loving brothers-in-law (?), pleasant, do thou
    worship (sapary) this householder’s fire.
Notes

Our mss. differ, as in the preceding verse, between devс╣Ы╠Бk─Бm─Б and
dev├бk- in c. The first three p─Бdas agree nearly with RV. x. 85. 44
a-c, but the latter begins a with ├бghoracakс╣гus (like our 17
a) тМКand omits ih├бтМЛ, reads sum├бn─Бs instead of suy├бm─Б in b,
and in c omits praj─Б╠Бvat─л and gives dev├бk─Бm─Б; its fourth p─Бda is
the commonplace phrase ┼Ы├бс╣Б no bhava dvip├бde ┼Ы├бс╣Б c├бtuс╣гpade. Ppp. reads
for a, b: adevaraghni patiraghny edhi syonaс╣г pa┼Ыubhyas sumanas
suv─лraс╕е; and, for c, d (given, as noted above, as second half of
the preceding verse): praj─Бvat─л v─лras┼лr devс╣Ыk─Бme тАЩmam agn- etc.; it
thus gets rid of the syon─Б whose apparent intrusion spoils the
triс╣гс╣нubh-character of our c, d. тМКThe ms. reckons syon─Б╠Б to d
(by placing the mark of p─Бda-division before it); but the integrity of
im├бm etc. as a p─Бda (without syon─Б╠Б) is palpable. Likely our text
represents a blend of two readings: v─лras┼л╠Бur dev├бk─Бm─Б sion─Б╠Б (RV.), and
praj─Б╠Бvat─л v─лras┼л╠Бr devс╣Ы╠Бk─Бm─Б (Ppp.): cf. under vs. 17.тАФPerhaps the
corruption at xviii. 1. 39 below is in part due to a confused blending
of two readings.тМЛ

Griffith

No slayer of thy husband or his father, gentle and bright, bring blessing on the cattle. Loving thy husband’s father, bring forth heroes. Tend well this household fire: be soft and pleasant.

Translation
  1. Stand up from here; desiring what hast thou (f.) come hither? I
    [am] thine overcomer, O Iс╕Н─Б, out of [my] own house; thou that hast
    come hither, O perdition, seeking the emptyтАФstand up, O niggard; fly
    forth; rest not here.

Griffith

Up and begone! What wish hath brought thee hither from thine own house? Thy mightier, I conjure thee. Vain is the hope, O Nirriti, that brought thee. Fly off, Malignity; stay here no longer.

Whitney
Translation
  1. When this bride hath worshiped the householder’s, the former
    (p┼л╠Бrva) fire, then, O woman, do thou pay homage to Sarasvat─л and to
    the Fathers.
Notes

Ppp. (which not rarely substitutes ─Бi for ─л) seems to agree with all
our mss. in reading asapary─Бit тМКsee the note to vi. 32. 2тМЛ. Pr─Бt. ii.
65 prescribes the combination n├бmas k- in d. The first p─Бda (10
syll.) is both irregular and defective. By K─Бu┼Ы. 77. 23, the ver.se,
with vs. 46 below, is to accompany the homage paid by the bride to the
deities mentioned.

Griffith

As first of all this woman hath adored the sacred household fire. So do thou, Dame, pay homage to the Fathers and Sarasvati.

Take thou this wrapper as a screen, to be a covering for the bride O Sinivali, let her bear children, and live in Bhaga’s grace.

реиреи рдпрдВ рдмрд▓реНрдмрдЬрдиреНрдиреНрдпрд╕реНрдпрде ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. What rushes (b├бlbaja) ye cast down, and [what] hide ye spread
    under, that let the girl (kany─Б╠А) of good progeny mount, who finds a
    husband.
Notes

Balbaja is the Eleusine indica, a coarse rush-like grass. In Ppp.,
the parts of vss. 22 and 23, and of 24 and 25, are more or less
exchanged. In K─Бu┼Ы. 78, the second p─Бda is first quoted (in 2), after
our vs. 21; then follows (in 3) a, then (in 4) the first part of vs.
23, then (in 5) our c, then (in 6) the second half of vs. 23, all
accompanying the corresponding acts of preparing a seat for the bride,
that she may take a Brahman-boy into her lap, to encourage the
obtainment of male progeny. It may be that Ppp. follows with its changed
order the succession of the acts as given in K─Бu┼Ы.

Griffith

Let her who shall be blest with sons, the maid who finds a. husband, step Upon the rough grass that ye spread and on the skin ye lay beneath.

  1. Spread under the rushes upon the red hide; sitting down upon it, of

Whitney
Translation
  1. Mount the hide; sit by the fire; this god slays all the demons; here
    give birth to progeny for this husband; may this son of thine be of good
    primogeniture.
Notes

The last p─Бda is used by K─Бu┼Ы. 78. 8 as the boy is seated in the bride’s
lap, though unsuited to the purpose unless forced out of its natural
meaning. тМКCf. Wint., p. 75.тМЛ There must be some error in the Anukr. text
relating to this verse and vs. 25 (which are triс╣гс╣нubh) and vs. 32 (see
below).

Griffith

Step on the skin and wait upon this Agni: he is the God who drives away all demons. Here bear thou children to this man thy husband: let this thy boy be happy in his birthnight.

Translation
  1. Let there come forth (vi-sth─Б) from the lap of this mother animals
    (pa┼Ы├║) of various forms, being born; as one of excellent omen, sit
    thou by this fire; with thy husband (s├бmpatn─л), be thou serviceable to
    the gods here.

In K─Бu┼Ы. 78. 9 this verse accompanies the removal of the boy again from
the bride’s lap. The verse is a pure triс╣гс╣нubh. тМКW. pencils the note
“cf. K. xxxix. 10."тМЛ

Griffith

Let many babes of varied form and nature spring in succession from this fruitful mother. Wait on this fire, thou bringer of good fortune. Here with thy husband serve the Gods with worship.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Of excellent omen, extender (prat├бraс╣Зa) of the houses, very
    propitious to thy husband, wealful to thy father-in-law, pleasant to thy
    mother-in-law, do thou enter these houses.
Notes

The comm. to Pr─Бt. iii. 60 notes the accent of ┼Ыva┼Ыrv─Б├н. The verse
seems to be overlooked altogether in the Anukr. as we have it; it should
be called a 3-p. vir─Бс╣З n─Бma g─Бyatr─л (11 + 11: 11 = 33). It is used
in K─Бu┼Ы. 77. 20 as the bride enters her new abode.

Griffith

Bliss-bringer, furthering thy household’s welfare, dear gladdening thy husband and his father, enter this home, mild to thy hus- band’s mother.

Griffith

Signs of good fortune mark the bride. Come all of you and look at her. Wish her prosperity: take on you her evil lucks and go your way.

Griffith

Surya the child of Savitar mounted for high felicity Her litter with its cloth of gold, wearing all forms of loveliness.

рейрез рдЖ рд░реЛрд╣ ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. Mount the couch with favoring mind; here give birth to progeny for
    this husband; like Indr─Бс╣З─л, waking with good awakening, mayest thou
    watch to meet dawns tipped with light.
Notes

Ppp. reads in c supt─Б for sub├║dh─Б, of which the stem and sense
are questionable (it occurs elsewhere only in vs. 75, below); at the end
it has c─Бkaraс╕е (for j─Бgaraс╕е). тМКCf. Wint, p. 92.тМЛ The excess of
syllables in d is a very poor reason for calling the verse (11 + 11:
11 + 13 = 46) a jagat─л. In K─Бu┼Ы. 76. 25 the verse is used, with 1. 60,
when the bride mounts the couch; and again, 79. 4, when she ascends the
nuptial bed (vs. 23 immediately follows: see above).

Griffith

Rise, mount the bridal bed with cheerful spirit. Here bring forth children to this man thy husband. Watchful and understanding like Indrani wake thou before the earliest light of Morning.

Whitney
Translation
  1. The gods in the beginning lay with (ni-pad) their spouses; they
    embraced (sam-spс╣Ы┼Ы) bodies with bodies; like S┼лry─Б, O woman,
    all-formed, with greatness, having progeny, unite (sam-bh┼л) here with
    thy husband.
Notes

Ppp. combines at the beginning dev─Б тАЩgre. The verse (11 + 11: 12 + 11
= 45) is almost a good triс╣гс╣нubh, in spite of the Anukr. тМКIt would be a
perfect triс╣гс╣нubh in cadence and otherwise if we had the right to
excise n─Бri, the intrusive character of which is very likely.тМЛ It is
used in K─Бu┼Ы. 79. 6 when the bride enters the nuptial bed; and also, in
75. 11, vss. 32-36 are strangely made to accompany the strewing of
grasses by the wooers who have gone out to arrange for the bridal.

Griffith

The Gods at first lay down beside their consorts; body with body met in close embracement. O Dame, like Surya perfect in her grandeur, here rich in future children, meet thy husband.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Stand up from here, O Vi┼Ыv─Бvasu; with homage do we praise thee; seek
    thou a sister (j─Бm├н) sitting among the Fathers, inserted (?
    ny├аkt─Бm); that is thy portion by right of birth; know thou that.
Notes

This verse corresponds to RV. x. 85. 22 a, b and 21 c, d; but
RV. reads at the beginning ├║d ─лrс╣гv─Б╠Б тАЩto vi┼Ы-; and in c any─Б╠Бm for
j─Бm├нm, and vy├аkt─Бm for ny├аkt─Бm, which seems a mere ignorant
substitution for it. Our mss. are divided between ny├аktam and -t─Бm;
I.E.p.m.O.s.m.R.T.D.K. give -t─Бm, which ending is doubtless to be
accepted as the true reading. Ppp. reads with RV. at the beginning, but

Griffith

Rise and go hence, Visvavasu: with reverence we worship thee. Steal to her sister dwelling with her father: this is the share– mark this–of old assigned thee.

Whitney
Translation
  1. The Apsarases revel a joint reveling, between the oblation-holder
    and the sun; they are thy birthplace; go away to them; homage I pay thee
    with the Gandharva-season.
Notes

The first half-verse is identical with vii. 109. 3 a, b. The verse,
a fairly good triс╣гс╣нubh, appears, with vss. 36 and 38, to be passed
over by the тМКLondonтМЛ Anukr. тМКThe Berlin ms. gives the three prat─лkas,
followed, without iti, by agastatakс╣гe (!).тМЛ Ppp. begins the verse
with y─Б тАЩpsarasas s- (for y─Б╠Б aps-), and in b puts antara (for
-r─Б) before havirdh─Бnam .

Griffith

Apsarases rejoice and feast together between the sun and place of sacrificing. These are thy kith and kin: go thou and join them: I in due season worship thee Gandharva.

Translation
  1. Homage to the Gandharva’s mind (?), and homage to his terrible
    (bh─Б╠Бma) eye we pay; O Vi┼Ыv─Бvasu, homage [be] to thee with worship
    (br├бhman); go away unto thy wives, the Apsarases.
Notes

The translation implies the naturally suggested emendation in a of
n├бmase to m├бnase, which Ppp. supports, reading manaso. Ppp. has
further bh─Бs─Бya for bh─Бm─Бya in b; and, for c, vi┼Ыv─Бvaso
namo brahmaс╣З─Б te kс╣Ыс╣Зomi, and, in d, combines j─Бy─Б тАЩps-. The
addition of тАШstu at the end of our c would rectify the meter of
the p─Бda and make the definition of the Anukr. exact.

Griffith

Homage we pay to the Gandharva’s favour, obeisance to his eye and fiery anger. Visvavasu, with prayer we pay thee homage. Go hence to those Apsarases thy consorts.

Whitney
Translation
  1. With wealth may we be well-willing; we have made the Gandharva go
    (vс╣Ыt) up from here; that god hath gone to the highest station
    (sadh├бstha); we have gone where they lengthen out [their] life-time.
Notes

The prefix ─Б╠Б in b seems out of place. The last p─Бda appears twice
in RV. (i. 113. 16 d; viii. 48. 11 d). The definition of the
verse (as noted under vs. 34) appears to be omitted in the Anukr. For
the application made in K─Бu┼Ы. of this and the preceding verses, see
under vs. 32; it does not seem at all suitable. Ppp. has in d for
yatra the variant vayam тМКimplying, perhaps, that the Kashmir
V─Бidikas understood pratir├бnta (p. praре░tir├бnte) as pratir├бntas.
тМКWith regard to an Anukr. statement that seems to concern this verse,
see above, p. 739, ┬╢’s 4, 5, 7.тМЛ

тМКCf. xviii. 2. 29 n.тМЛ

Griffith

May we be happy with abundant riches. We from this place have banished the Gandharva. The God is gone to the remotest region, and we have come where men prolong existence.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Unite (sam-sс╣Ыj), O ye (two) parents (pitс╣Ы╠Б), the (two) things
    that are seasonable; ye shall be mother and father of seed; as a male
    (m├бrya) a female (y├│с╣г─Б), do thou mount her; make ye (two) progeny;
    here enjoy (puс╣г) wealth.
Notes

тМКFor “mount her,” W. suggests in pencil “make her mount”; but I suspect
that the full expression would be ├бdhi rohaya ┼Ы├йpa en─Бm. In a,
с╣Ы╠Бtviye is regarded by the pada-text as dual, and is translated
accordingly; it probably means the respective contributions of the two
to the embryo. Ppp. reads instead (-r─Б) vс╣Ыddhaye, a welcome
emendation. Further, in b, it puts pit─Б, before m─Бt─Б and has
ja for ca and ends b with bhav─Бtha; тМКand it makes our 37
d and 39 c change place, but with puс╣гyatu no for our
puс╣гyatamтМЛ. тМКPronounce m├бryeva in c: the verse then scans easily
as 11 + 11: 11 + 12, if we accept the resolution с╣Ы╠Бtuiye in a.тМЛ
According to K─Бu┼Ы. 79. 8, it is used in the act of coition. тМКConcerning
the matter as an essential element of the ritual, see Winternitz, p.
92.тМЛ Ppp. arranges this and the following six verses in the order 37,
40, 38, 39, 42, 41. 43.

Griffith

In your due season, Parents! come together. Mother and sire be ye of future children. Embrace this woman like a happy lover. Raise ye up offspring here: increase your riches.

Griffith

Send her most rich in every charm, O Pushan, her who shall be the sharer of my pleasures; Her who shall twine her eager arms about me, and welcome all my love and soft embraces.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Mount thou the thigh; apply the hand; embrace thy wife with
    well-willing mind; make ye (two) progeny here, enjoying; let Savitar
    make for you a long life-time.
Notes

The first half-verse is found also in the ─Аpast. text (Wint., p. 90 тМКMP.
i. 11. 7тМЛ), with the variant (after ┼лr├║m) ├║pa barhasva b─Бh├║m. тМКPpp.,
as just noted, makes our 37 d change place with our 39 c,
reading, however, rodam─Бn─Бu for mod-; and in its d it has tu
for v─Бm, combining tv ─Бyus sav-.тМЛ The verse is ill defined as a
jagat─л or bhurik triс╣гс╣нubh; it is properly a svar─Бс╣н triс╣гс╣нubh.

Griffith

Up, happy bridegroom! with a joyous spirit caress thy wife and throw thine arm around her. Here take your pleasure, procreate your offspring. May Savitar bestow long life upon you.

MS. (ii. 13. 23) has p─Бda a only. The verse is almost a good jagat─л,
only a little damaged by the intrusion of imam in c; тМКand a
perfect jagat─л, if (with RV. MB. MP.) we omit imamтМЛ.

Griffith

So may the Lord of Life vouchsafe you children, Aryaman bind you, day and night, together. Enter thy husband’s house with happy omens, bring blessing to our quadrupeds and bipeds.

Whitney
Translation
  1. This bridal garment and bride’s dress, given by the gods together
    with Manu, whoso gives to a knowing (cikitv─Б╠Бс╣Еs) priest (brahm├бn), he
    verily slays the demons of the couch (?).
Notes

The translation implies at the end the emendation (suggested also by
Weber, p. 211) of t├бlp─Бni to t├бlpy─Бni, as required by both sense and
meter, and supported by the Ppp. reading tс╣Ыpy─Бni. For b, Ppp.
gives v─Бdh┼лyaс╣Б baddho (vadhvo?) v─Бso тАШsy─Бс╕е, which, though metrically
awkward, is not redundant in expression. In K─Бu┼Ы. 79. 21, the verse
accompanies the priest’s acceptance of the bridal garment, given him
with 1. 25. The verse is a good triс╣гс╣нubh, if emended as proposed in
d. тМКCf. vii. 37. 1 n.тМЛ

Griffith

Sent by the Gods associate with Manu, the vesture of the bride, the nuptial garment, He who bestows this on a thoughtful Brahman, drives from the marriage-bed all evil demons.

Whitney
Translation
  1. What priest’s portion they (dual) give to me the bride-seeker
    (vadh┼лy├║), the bridal garment and bride’s dress, do ye, O Brihaspati
    and Indra, assenting, together give it to the priest (brahm├бn).
Notes

The anomalous accent datt├бm at the end is read by all our тМКand SPP’sтМЛ
authorities. Ppp. varies considerably: yan no тАШditi brahmabh─Бgaс╣Б
vadh┼лyor v─Бso vadhva┼Ы ca vastram; and dhatt─Бm at the end.

Griffith

The priestly meed wherewith ye twain present me, the vesture of the bride, the nuptial garment, This do ye both, Brihaspati and Indra, bestow with loving-kind- ness on the Brahman.

рдпрдореНред рдореЗреТред рджреТрддреНрддрдГред рдмреНрд░реТрд╣реНрдореТрд╜рднрд╛реТрдЧрдореНред рд╡реТрдзреВреТрд╜рдпреЛрдГред рд╡рд╛рдзреВреСрд╜рдпрдореНред рд╡рд╛рд╕рдГреСред рд╡реТрдзреНрд╡рдГс│бред рдЪреТред рд╡рд╕реНрддреНрд░реСрдореНред рдпреБреТрд╡рдореНред рдмреНрд░реТрд╣реНрдордгреЗреСред рдЕреТрдиреБреТрд╜рдордиреНрдпреСрдорд╛рдиреМред рдмреГрд╣реСрд╕реНрдкрддреЗред рд╕рд╛реТрдХрдореНред рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдГреСред рдЪреТред рджреТрддреНрддрдореНред реи.рекреиред

Whitney
Translation
  1. Awaking out of a pleasant lair (y├│ni), mightily enjoying
    yourselves, merry, having good kine, good sons, good houses, may ye,
    living, pass the outshining dawns.
Notes

Ppp. reads in c, d subh─Бu suputr─Бu sukс╣Ыt─Бu car─Бt─Бu j─лv─Б uс╣г-; our
P.M.W. have car─Бtho. To accent t├бr─Бthas, counting it to d
instead of c, would be an improvement. The verse (which scans 11 +
11: 8 + 11 or 11 + 8 = 41) is very ill described by the Anukr. According
to K─Бu┼Ы. 79. 12, it accompanies the rising from the nuptial bed.

Griffith

On your soft couch awaking both together, revelling heartily with joy and laughter, Rich with brave sons, good cattle, goodly homestead, live long to look on many radiant mornings.

Notes

Ppp. combines a-b suv─Бso тАЩd─Б-. According to K─Бu┼Ы. 79. 27, the
verse is used when the priest comes back after washing the bridal
garment.

Griffith

Clad in new garments, fragrant, well-apparelled, to meet reful- gent Dawn have I arisen. I, like a bird that quits the egg, am freed from sin and purified.

Whitney
Translation

45 . Beautiful [are] heaven-and-earth, pleasant near by, of great
courses; seven divine waters have flowed; let them free us from
distress.

Notes

This verse is a repetition of vii. 112. 1. Ppp. reads in b
yantusumne, and, for c, ─Бpas sapta sravant─лs (t─Б etc.). The
redundant syllable in c is not noticed by the Anukr. here, although
it was so at the other occurrence. The verse is used by K─Бu┼Ы. 78. 10
with vs. 1 (see the note to that verse), and again in 78. 13 it
accompanies the pouring of water into the folded hands of the pair; and
yet again, in 79. 25, the pouring of water on the bridal garment; this
use is evidently the one which gives the verse its place here.

Griffith

Splendid are Heaven and Earth, still near to bless us, mighty in their power; The seven streams have flowed: may they, Goddesses, free us from distress

Whitney
Translation
  1. How many witchcrafts in the outer garment (? upav─Б╠Бsana), how many
    fetters of king Varuс╣Зa, what failures, what non-successesтАФthem I cause
    to sit upon this pillar.
Notes

Ppp. has pa┼Ыc─Бc─Бne in a for upav─Бsane; and, for d, asmin t─Б
st─Бno mu├▒c─Бmi sarv─Бm. Our P.M.W. read in d t─Б╠Бс╣Б sth-; the rest,
t─Б╠Бс╕е sth-. In K─Бu┼Ы. 79. 23 the verse is used immediately after the
preceding. The lack of a syllable in a is disregarded by the Anukr.

Griffith

All witcheries that hang about this garment, all royal Varuna’s entangling nooses. All failure of success and all misfortunes here I deposit fastened to the pillar.

Whitney
Translation
  1. What is my dearest self (tan┼л╠Б), that of me is afraid of the
    garment; of it do thou, O forest-lord, make first (├бgre) for thyself
    an inner wrap (n─лv├н); let us not suffer harm.
Notes

This verse is used in K─Бu┼Ы. 79. 24 next after the two preceding, the
person who has the garment in charge wrapping a tree with it. The Anukr.
contains no definition of the meter (8 + 8: 8 + 11 = 35). The verse, as
noted above, is wanting in Ppp.

Griffith

My body that I hold most dear trembles in terror at this robe. Tree, make an apron at the top. Let no misfortune fall on us.

Whitney
Translation
  1. If these hairy people have danced together in thy house, doing evil
    with wailingтАФfrom that sin let Agni and Savitar release thee.
Notes

This and the three following verses are discussed by Bloomfield in AJP.
xi. 336 ff. тМКor JAOS. xv., p. xliv. = PAOS. for Oct. 1890тМЛ. They
evidently have no connection originally with marriage ceremonies, but
rather with wailings for the dead, which are regarded as ill-omened and
requiring expiation.* тМКCf. the following verses.тМЛ K─Бu┼Ы. quotes only
this one (79. 30), and for no definite purpose, combining it with 1. 46
(see note to the latter). Ppp. reads in a yad am─л for yad─л тАЩme,
and in c kс╣Ыс╣Зvat─лs. The false accent kс╣Ыс╣Зvant├бs (which our edition
has not corrected) is read by all our mss. save one (D.).

тМКThe case is nearly the same with the authorities of SPP., who says,
“This reading [kс╣Ыс╣Зvant├│] appears ancient, traditional, and general.”
A note in my copy of AV. suggests that the blunder may have crept in
from vs. 61; and I find my surmise confirmed not only by SPP. (who,
however, attributes the wrong accent and kampa to vs. 60; see his
note), but also by the fact of similar occurrences elsewhere: cf., for
example, the curious avagraha of s├бmре░j├▒apay─Бmi at vi. 74. 2 (and my
note); the impossible v├нре░bh─Бti at xiii. 3. 17, and note; etc.тМЛ

*тМКCf. Francis James Child, The English and Scottish Popular Ballads,
part x., p. 498, under the heading “Tears destroy the peace of the
dead,” and the citation from MBh. xi. 1. 42-43 given on p. 294 of the
same part: “For they [the tears], like sparks, ’tis said, do burn
those men [for whom they’re shed]."тМЛ тМКSee L├╝ders, ZDMG. lviii. 507.тМЛ

Griffith

Translation
  1. If in thy progeny, in thy cattle, or in thy houses is settled
    (ni-sth─Б) any evil done by the evil-doersтАФfrom that sin etc. etc.

Griffith

If any evil have been wrought by mischief-makers that affects thy cattle progeny or house, May Agni free thee from the woe, may Savitar deliver thee.

Whatever magic hath been wrought on cushion, chair, or canopy. Each spell to mar the wedding rites, all this we throw into the bath.

We, having laid the stain and fault upon the interceder’s cloak, Are pure and meet for sacrifice. May he prolong our lives for us.

Whitney
Translation
  1. The artificial hundred-toothed comb (?) that is here shall scratch
    away the defilement of the hair of her, away that of her head.
Notes

The majority of our mss. (all but Bs.s.m.P.R.) read k├бс╣Зс╣нakas ’thorn’
in a. Ppp. has kan╠Дkadas. The K─Бu┼Ы. text, 76. 5, with the
subsidiary texts (see note to that rule), gives kan╠Дkata, with our
edition. There is little to choose between the two readings. Ppp. reads
in b ap─Б тАЩsy─Бt k-. The verse, which is a purauс╣гс╣Зih, is not
defined by the Anukr. K─Бu┼Ы. 76. 5 makes it accompany the combing of the
bride’s hair after she has been bathed and (with 1. 45, 53) clothed in a
new garment.

Griffith

Now let this artificial comb, wrought with a hundred teeth, remove Aught of impurity that dims the hair upon this woman’s head.

Translation
  1. Away from every limb of her do we deposit the y├бkс╣гma; let that not
    attain (pra-─Бp) the earth nor the gods; let it not attain the heaven,
    the wide atmosphere; let that defilement not attain the waters, O Agni;
    let it not attain Yama and all the Fathers.
Notes

Ppp. reads in a, b yo тАШyam asy─Бm upa yakс╣гmaс╣Б ni dhatta naс╕е. K─Бu┼Ы.
76. 14 uses the verse to accompany the purifying of the bride. The
metrical structure (8 + 8: 11 + 11: 11 + 11 = 60) is described as well
as the Anukr. knows how.

Griffith

We take away consumption from each limb and member of the bride. Let not this reach Earth, nor the Gods in heaven, let it not reach the sky or air’s wide region. Let not this dust that sullies reach the Waters, nor Yama, Agni, nor the host of Fathers.

Griffith

With all the milk that is in Earth I gird thee, with all the milk that Plants contain I dress thee. I gird thee round with children and with riches. Do thou, thus girt, receive the offered treasure.

Whitney
Translation
  1. He am I, she thou; chant am I, verse thou; heaven I, earth thou; let
    us (two) come together here; let us generate progeny.
Notes

The verse (8 + 8 + 8: 7 + 8 = 39) is strangely called a bс╣Ыhat─л by the
Anukr. It is found, with more or less variation, in a host of other
texts: AB. (viii. 27. 4), TB. (iii. 7.1тБ╣), K. (xxxv. 18), ┼ЫB. (xiv. 9.
4┬╣тБ╣), AGS. (i. 7. 6), PCS. (i. 6. 3), HGS. (i. 20. 2), ─Аp. (ix. 2. 3).
In the first p─Бda, TB. (with which HGS. and ─Аp. agree throughout) has
the unintelligent reading ├бm┼лh├бm; AB. has sa for s─Б, which seems
also a mere blunder. After this, AB.┼ЫB.AGS.PGS. add the same, inverted:
s─Б╠Б (AB. sa again) tv├бm asy ├бmo тАШh├бm (┼ЫB. PGS. ah├бm). As regards
our third p─Бda, there is no variant in reading, but AB.TB.AGS.HGS.─Аp.
put it before our second. In our second p─Бda, the same texts omit the
asmi; the whole p─Бda is wanting in Ppp. For our d, AB. has t─Бv
eha saс╣Б vah─Бvah─Бi, and ends there; TB. etc. give as ending to the verse
t─Б╠Бv ├й тАЩhi s├бm bhav─Бva sah├б r├йto dadh─Бvah─Бi puс╣Бs├й putr─Б╠Бya v├йttav─Бi;
┼ЫB. nearly the same, but with saс╣Бrabh─Б╠Бvah─Бi, dadh─Б╠Бvah─Бi, and
v├нttaye; AGS. instead t─Бv e тАЩhe vi vah─Бvah─Бi praj─Бm pra janay─Бvah─Бi;
PGS. spins out the longest ending: t─Бv e тАЩhi vi vah─Бvah─Бi saha reto
dadh─Бvah─Бi praj─Бm pra janay─Бvah─Бi putr─Бn vind─Бvah─Бi bah┼лn te santu
jaradaс╣гс╣нayaс╕е. тМКCf. MP. i. 3. 14, and Wint., p. 52; also MGS. i. 10. 15
d, and p. 146, and i. 10. 15 e, and p. 150, s.v. t─Б; also GB. ii. 3.
20; JUB. i. 54.тМЛ K─Бu┼Ы. 79. 10 uses the verse, with i. 34. 1, after the

Griffith

I am this man, that dame art thou I am the psalm and thou the verse. I am the heaven and thou the earth. So will we dwell together here, parents of children yet to be.

Whitney
Translation
  1. The unmarried of us seek a wife, the liberal seek a son; may we
    (two), with uninjured life-breath, be companions (sac), in order to
    what is great, to winning of strength (? v─Б╠Бja-).

emendation to nas or to n├║. The corresponding half-verse in RV.

putr─лy├бntaс╕е s-. That our denominatives have a right to their short i
is further vouched for by their quotation as examples for it under Pr─Бt.
iii. 18. Whether one should emend in d to bс╣Ыhaty─Бi, or translate
as is done above, may be made a question; it seems most likely to be a
mixed construction, meaning virtually ‘in order to the gaining of great
v─Бja.’ V─Б╠Бjas─Бtaye is never joined with an adjective in RV. Ppp.
reads with our text throughout.

Griffith

Unmarried men desire to wed; bountiful givers wish for sons. Together may we dwell with strength unscathed for high pros- perity.

Whitney
Translation
  1. What bride-beholding Fathers have come to this bridal-car, let them
    bestow on this bride, with her husband, protection accompanied with
    progeny.
Notes

The pada-text has the bad reading ─Б╠Б: agaman, instead of ─Бре░├бgaman.
Part of our mss. (Bp.P.M.W.O.) read in c s├бmpaty─Бi, but doubtless
only by the scribes’ oversight. According to K─Бu┼Ы. 77. 12, the verse is
to be used when the bridal train passes by a burial-place.

Griffith

May they, the Fathers who, to view the bride, have joined this nuptial train, Grant to this lady and her lord children and peaceful happiness.

Translation
  1. She who hath come hither before, girdling herself (?), having given
    to this woman here progeny and propertyтАФher let them carry along the
    road of what is not gone; this one, a vir─Б╠Бj, having good progeny, hath

Notes

This obscure verse is not made clear by K─Бu┼Ы. 77. 4; though the latter
perhaps means it to be used if another bridal procession goes athwart
the track at a cross-roads. The pada-text in a divides without any
reason ra┼Ыan─Бре░y├бm─Бn─Б. Perhaps, too, we ought to resolve p┼л╠Бrv─Б╠Бgan
into p┼л╠Бrv─Б: ─Бре░├бgan, instead of p┼л╠Бrv─Б: ├бgan, as the p. does. The
third p─Бda is perhaps a mere ill-wish with contempt: ‘she may go to
grass.’ Ppp. reads in b dhatt─Бm, in c abhi for anu, and
combines in d supraj─Б тАЩty-. тМКFor consistency, the Berlin text
should have dattv─Б╠Б.тМЛ

Griffith

Her who first guided by a rein came hither, giving the bride, here offspring and possessions, Let them convey along the future’s pathway. Splendid, with noble children, she hath conquered.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Continue thou awake, waking with good awakening, unto length of life
    of a hundred autumns; go to the houses that thou mayest be
    house-mistress; let Savitar make for thee a long life-time.
Notes

Ppp. reads for c gс╣Ыh─Бn pre тАЩhi sumanasyam─Бn─Б, and combines in

Griffith

Wake to long life, watchful and understanding, yea, to a life shall last a hundred autumns Enter the house to be the household’s mistress. A long long life let Savitar vouchsafe thee.

рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдгреА: ренрелтИТ(рдкреНрд░рдмреБрдзреНрдпрд╕реНрд╡) рдкреНрд░рдХрд░реНрд╖реЗрдг рдЬрд╛рдЧреГрддрд╛ рд╡рд░реНрддрд╕реНрд╡ (рд╕реБрдмреБрдзрд╛) рдЙрддреНрддрдордмреБрджреНрдзрд┐рдорддреА (рдмреБрдзреНрдпрдорд╛рдирд╛)рд╕рд╛рд╡рдзрд╛рдирд╛ (рджреАрд░реНрдШрд╛рдпреБрддреНрд╡рд╛рдп) рджреАрд░реНрдШрдЬреАрд╡рдирдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддрдпреЗ (рд╢рддрд╢рд╛рд░рджрд╛рдп) рд╢рддрд╡рд░реНрд╖рдпреБрдХреНрддрд╛рдп (рдЧреГрд╣рд╛рдиреН)рдЧреГрд╣рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреН (рдЧрдЪреНрдЫ) рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреБрд╣рд┐ (рдЧреГрд╣рдкрддреНрдиреА) рдЧреГрд╣рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдорд┐рдирдВ (рдпрдерд╛) рдпреЗрди рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░реЗрдг (рдЕрд╕рдГ) рддреНрд╡рдВ рднрд╡реЗрдГ (рджреАрд░реНрдШрдореН) (рддреЗ) рддрд╡ (рдЖрдпреБрдГ) рдЬреАрд╡рдирдореН (рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛) рдкрд░рдореИрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдЬрдЧрджреАрд╢реНрд╡рд░рдГ (рдХреГрдгреЛрддреБ) рдХрд░реЛрддреБ рее
